release of the "Alternate Realities" box set, remastered <i>Original Series</i> episodes were included in a multi-series compilation for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<p>While still casting the roles, Gene Roddenberry had mandated that Bones McCoy and Spock be male. According to Nichelle Nichols, "They gave me a three-page script to read from that had three characters named Bones, Kirk and somebody called Spock, and they asked me if I would read for the role of Spock. When I looked at this great text, I said to myself, 'I'll take any one of these roles,' but I found the Spock character to be very interesting, and I asked them to tell me what she [Spock] was like". They then told Nichols that the role had already been offered to Leonard Nimoy.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>It was intended that Sulu's role be expanded in the second season, but owing to Takei's part in John Wayne's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Green_Berets_(film)" title="The Green Berets (film)">The Green Berets</a></i>, he appeared in only half the season, his role being filled by <a href="/wiki/Walter_Koenig" title="Walter Koenig">Walter Koenig</a> as the relatively young, <a href="/wiki/Mop-top" class="mw-redirect" title="Mop-top">mop-topped</a> Russian navigator Ensign <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Chekov" title="Pavel Chekov">Pavel Chekov</a>. When Takei returned, the two had to share a dressing room.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The two appeared together at the <i>Enterprise</i> helm for the remainder of the series. There may be some truth to the unofficial story that the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>'s newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Pravda" title="Pravda">Pravda</a></i> complained that among the culturally diverse characters there were no Russians, seen as a personal slight to that country since the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Soviet Russian</a> <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">Yuri Gagarin</a> had been the first man to make a spaceflight. Gene Roddenberry said in response that "The Chekov thing was a major error on our part, and I'm still embarrassed by the fact we didn't include a Russian right from the beginning."<sup id="cite_ref-whitfield1968_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whitfield1968-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, documentation from Desilu suggests that the intention was to introduce a character into <i>Star Trek</i> with more sex appeal to teenaged girls.<sup id="cite_ref-whitfield1968_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whitfield1968-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Walter Koenig noted in the 2006 40th anniversary special of <i>Star Trek: The Original Series</i> that he doubted the rumor about <i>Pravda</i>, since <i>Star Trek</i> had never been shown on Soviet television. It has also been claimed that the former member of <a href="/wiki/The_Monkees" title="The Monkees">The Monkees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Davy_Jones_(actor)" class="mw-redirect" title="Davy Jones (actor)">Davy Jones</a>, was the model for Mr. Chekov.<sup id="cite_ref-snopes_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snopes-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In addition, the series frequently included characters (usually security personnel wearing red uniforms) who are killed or injured soon after their introduction. So prevalent was this <a href="/wiki/Plot_device" title="Plot device">plot device</a> that it inspired the term "<a href="/wiki/Redshirt_(stock_character)" title="Redshirt (stock character)">redshirt</a>" to denote a <a href="/wiki/Stock_character" title="Stock character">stock character</a> whose sole purpose is to die violently in order to show the danger facing the main characters.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Characterizations">Characterizations</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Characterizations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:ST_TOS_Cast.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2d/ST_TOS_Cast.jpg/250px-ST_TOS_Cast.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="187" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/2/2d/ST_TOS_Cast.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="365" data-file-height="273" /></a><figcaption>Promotional photo of the cast of <i>Star Trek</i> during the third season (1968–1969). From left to right: <a href="/wiki/James_Doohan" title="James Doohan">James Doohan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Koenig" title="Walter Koenig">Walter Koenig</a>, <a href="/wiki/DeForest_Kelley" title="DeForest Kelley">DeForest Kelley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Majel_Barrett" title="Majel Barrett">Majel Barrett</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Shatner" title="William Shatner">William Shatner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nichelle_Nichols" title="Nichelle Nichols">Nichelle Nichols</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Nimoy" title="Leonard Nimoy">Leonard Nimoy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/George_Takei" title="George Takei">George Takei</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p><i>Star Trek</i> made celebrities of its cast of largely unknown actors. Kelley had appeared in many films and television shows, but mostly in smaller roles that showcased him as a villain. Nimoy also had previous television and film experience but was not well known either. Nimoy had partnered previously with Shatner in a 1964 episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_from_U.N.C.L.E." title="The Man from U.N.C.L.E.">The Man from U.N.C.L.E.</a></i>, "The Project Strigas Affair", and with Kelley (as a doctor) in a 1963 episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Virginian_(TV_series)" title="The Virginian (TV series)">The Virginian</a></i>, "Man of Violence", both more than two years before <i>Star Trek</i> first aired. Before <i>Star Trek</i>, Shatner was well known in the trade, having appeared in several notable films, played <a href="/wiki/Cyrano_de_Bergerac_(play)" title="Cyrano de Bergerac (play)">Cyrano de Bergerac</a> on Broadway, and even turned down the part of <a href="/wiki/Dr._Kildare_(TV_series)" title="Dr. Kildare (TV series)">Dr. Kildare</a>. However, when roles became sparse he took the regular job after Jeffrey Hunter's contract was not renewed.
</p><p>After the original series ended, cast members found themselves <a href="/wiki/Typecasting_(acting)" class="mw-redirect" title="Typecasting (acting)">typecast</a> because of their defining roles in the show. (<i>Star Trek: The Next Generation</i> actor <a href="/wiki/Michael_Dorn" title="Michael Dorn">Michael Dorn</a> stated in 1991, however: "If what happened to the first cast is called being typecast, then I want to be typecast. Of course, they didn't get the jobs after <i>Trek</i>. But they are making their sixth movie. Name me someone else in television who has made <i>six</i> movies!")<sup id="cite_ref-teitelbaum19910505_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teitelbaum19910505-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The three main characters were Kirk, Spock, and McCoy, with writers often playing the different personalities off each other: Kirk was passionate and often aggressive, but with a sly sense of humor; Spock was coolly logical; and McCoy was sardonic, emotional, and illogical, but always compassionate. In many stories the three clashed, with Kirk forced to make a tough decision while Spock advocated the logical but sometimes callous path and McCoy (or "Bones", as Kirk nicknamed him) insisted on doing whatever would cause the least harm. McCoy and Spock had a sparring relationship that masked their true affection and respect for each other, and their constant arguments became popular with viewers.<sup id="cite_ref-rioux2005_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rioux2005-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 153–154">&#58;&#8202;153–154&#8202;</span></sup> The show so emphasized dialogue that writer and director <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Meyer" title="Nicholas Meyer">Nicholas Meyer</a> (involved with the <i>Star Trek</i> films) called it a <a href="/wiki/Radio_drama" title="Radio drama">radio drama</a>, playing an episode for a film class without video to prove that the plot was still comprehensible.<sup id="cite_ref-teitelbaum19910505_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teitelbaum19910505-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Spock character was at first rejected by network executives, who were apprehensive that his vaguely "Satanic" appearance (with pointed ears and eyebrows) might prove upsetting to some viewers, and (according to Leonard Nimoy) they repeatedly urged Roddenberry to "drop the Martian". Roddenberry was also dismayed to discover that NBC's publicity department deliberately airbrushed out Spock's pointed ears and eyebrows from early publicity stills sent to network affiliates, because they feared that his "demonic" appearance might offend potential buyers in the religiously conservative southern states. Spock, however, went on to become one of the most popular characters on the show, as did McCoy's impassioned country-doctor personality. Spock, in fact, became a <a href="/wiki/Sex_symbol" title="Sex symbol">sex symbol</a> of sorts<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>—something no one connected with the show had expected. Leonard Nimoy noted that the question of Spock's extraordinary sex appeal emerged "almost any time I talked to someone in the press<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... I never give it a thought<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... to try to deal with the question of Mr. Spock as a sex symbol is silly."<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Characters'_cameo_appearances_in_later_series"><span id="Characters.27_cameo_appearances_in_later_series"></span>Characters' cameo appearances in later series</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Characters&#039; cameo appearances in later series"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The sequel to the original series, <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation" title="Star Trek: The Next Generation">Star Trek: The Next Generation</a></i>, which premiered in 1987, was set about 100 years after the events of <i>TOS</i>. As that show and its spin-offs progressed, several <i>TOS</i> actors made appearances reprising their original characters:
</p>
<ul><li>James Kirk disappears in 2293 during the maiden voyage of the <a href="/wiki/USS_Enterprise_(NCC-1701-B)" class="mw-redirect" title="USS Enterprise (NCC-1701-B)"><i>Enterprise</i>-B</a> as seen in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_Generations" title="Star Trek Generations">Star Trek: Generations</a></i>. However, now chronologically 138 years old, but still only physically 60 years old, Kirk is recovered after spending 78 years in <a href="/wiki/The_Nexus_(Star_Trek)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Nexus (Star Trek)">The Nexus</a>, an alternative plane of existence, by <i>Enterprise</i>-D Captain Jean-Luc Picard in the same film. Kirk's time in the 24th century is short, however; he is killed while helping to defeat Dr. <a href="/wiki/Tolian_Soran" class="mw-redirect" title="Tolian Soran">Tolian Soran</a>.</li>
<li>Spock, now a <a href="/wiki/Vulcan_(Star_Trek_planet)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vulcan (Star Trek planet)">Vulcan</a> ambassador, goes underground in the <a href="/wiki/Romulan_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Romulan Empire">Romulan Empire</a> in hopes of fostering peaceful coexistence with the <a href="/wiki/United_Federation_of_Planets" title="United Federation of Planets">Federation</a> and reunification with Vulcan society ("<a href="/wiki/Unification_(Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation)" title="Unification (Star Trek: The Next Generation)">Unification, Parts I and II</a>"). He also appears in the 2009 reboot film where his science vessel originated from the 24th century–era of TNG. He ends up stranded in the 23rd century of the film series, where he settles on new Vulcan; in the sequel film <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_Into_Darkness" title="Star Trek Into Darkness">Star Trek Into Darkness</a></i>, he is contacted by his younger self regarding the villainous <a href="/wiki/Khan_Noonien_Singh" title="Khan Noonien Singh">Khan Noonien Singh</a>. While not appearing in <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_Beyond" title="Star Trek Beyond">Star Trek Beyond</a></i>, it is mentioned in the film that the character has died, as an homage to the real-life passing of actor <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Nimoy" title="Leonard Nimoy">Leonard Nimoy</a>.</li>
<li>Leonard "Bones" McCoy, now a crusty 137-year-old admiral and head of Starfleet's Medical Division, inspects the <a href="/wiki/USS_Enterprise_(NCC-1701-D)" title="USS Enterprise (NCC-1701-D)"><i>Enterprise</i>-D</a> before her first mission in "<a href="/wiki/Encounter_at_Farpoint" title="Encounter at Farpoint">Encounter at Farpoint</a>", briefly meeting the android officer <a href="/wiki/Data_(Star_Trek)" title="Data (Star Trek)">Lt. Cdr. Data</a>, telling him, "Well, this is a new ship. But she's got the right name. Now, you remember that, you hear?<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... You treat her like a lady, and she'll always bring you home."</li>
<li>Montgomery Scott, now chronologically 147 years old, but still only physically 72 years old after spending 75 years trapped in a transporter buffer, is rescued by the <i>Enterprise</i>-D crew and resumes his life in "<a href="/wiki/Relics_(Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation)" title="Relics (Star Trek: The Next Generation)">Relics</a>". Working along with Chief Engineer <a href="/wiki/Geordi_La_Forge" title="Geordi La Forge">Geordi La Forge</a>, Scotty uses some creative engineering to save the <i>Enterprise</i>. A grateful Captain Picard lends him a shuttlecraft indefinitely.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sarek" title="Sarek">Sarek</a>, Spock's father, continues to be an ambassador for the next century until his final mission during which he and Captain Picard mind-meld together because Sarek shows signs of Bendii Syndrome ("Sarek"). He later dies suffering from this affliction, but not before giving <a href="/wiki/Jean-Luc_Picard" title="Jean-Luc Picard">Captain Picard</a> key information for locating his missing son ("Unification").</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kang_(Star_Trek)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kang (Star Trek)">Kang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Koloth" class="mw-redirect" title="Koloth">Koloth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kor_(Star_Trek)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kor (Star Trek)">Kor</a>, the three Klingons featured in "<a href="/wiki/Day_of_the_Dove" title="Day of the Dove">Day of the Dove</a>" (Kang), "<a href="/wiki/The_Trouble_with_Tribbles" title="The Trouble with Tribbles">The Trouble with Tribbles</a>" (Koloth) and "<a href="/wiki/Errand_of_Mercy" title="Errand of Mercy">Errand of Mercy</a>" (Kor), continue to serve the Empire well into the 24th century. They appear in the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Deep_Space_Nine" title="Star Trek: Deep Space Nine">Star Trek: Deep Space Nine</a></i> episode "<a href="/wiki/Blood_Oath_(Star_Trek:_Deep_Space_Nine)" title="Blood Oath (Star Trek: Deep Space Nine)">Blood Oath</a>" in which Kang and Koloth are killed. Kor later appears in two more episodes: "<a href="/wiki/The_Sword_of_Kahless" title="The Sword of Kahless">The Sword of Kahless</a>" and finally in "<a href="/wiki/Once_More_Unto_the_Breach_(Star_Trek:_Deep_Space_Nine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Once More Unto the Breach (Star Trek: Deep Space Nine)">Once More Unto the Breach</a>" where, fighting in the Dominion War, he dies honorably in battle. A younger version of Kang, from the era of <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_VI:_The_Undiscovered_Country" title="Star Trek VI: The Undiscovered Country">Star Trek VI: The Undiscovered Country</a></i>, later appears in the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Voyager" title="Star Trek: Voyager">Star Trek: Voyager</a></i> episode "<a href="/wiki/Flashback_(Star_Trek:_Voyager)" title="Flashback (Star Trek: Voyager)">Flashback</a>".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hikaru_Sulu" title="Hikaru Sulu">Hikaru Sulu</a>, promoted to captain of USS <i>Excelsior</i> in <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_VI:_The_Undiscovered_Country" title="Star Trek VI: The Undiscovered Country">Star Trek VI: The Undiscovered Country</a></i>, reprises his role from that performance in the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Voyager" title="Star Trek: Voyager">Star Trek: Voyager</a></i> episode "Flashback". <a href="/wiki/Janice_Rand" title="Janice Rand">Janice Rand</a> also appears in that same episode.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arne_Darvin" class="mw-redirect" title="Arne Darvin">Arne Darvin</a>, the Klingon disguised as a human in "<a href="/wiki/The_Trouble_with_Tribbles" title="The Trouble with Tribbles">The Trouble with Tribbles</a>", appears in the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Deep_Space_Nine" title="Star Trek: Deep Space Nine">Star Trek: Deep Space Nine</a></i> episode "<a href="/wiki/Trials_and_Tribble-ations" title="Trials and Tribble-ations">Trials and Tribble-ations</a>" with the intent to return to Deep Space Station K7 in 2267 and assassinate Kirk, whom Darvin blamed for his disgrace in the Klingon Empire.</li></ul>
<p>Besides the above examples, numerous non-canon novels and comic books have been published over the years in which <i>The Original Series</i> era crew are depicted in <i>The Next Generation</i> era, either through time-travel or other means. In addition, many actors who appeared on <i>The Original Series</i> later made guest appearances as different characters in later series, most notably <a href="/wiki/Majel_Barrett" title="Majel Barrett">Majel Barrett</a>, who not only provided the voice for most Starfleet computers in episodes of every spin-off series (including a single appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Enterprise" title="Star Trek: Enterprise">Star Trek: Enterprise</a></i>, where the computers normally did not speak at all), but also had the recurring role of <a href="/wiki/Lwaxana_Troi" class="mw-redirect" title="Lwaxana Troi">Lwaxana Troi</a> in <i>The Next Generation</i> and <i>Deep Space Nine</i>. <a href="/wiki/Diana_Muldaur" title="Diana Muldaur">Diana Muldaur</a>, a guest star in the episodes "<a href="/wiki/Return_to_Tomorrow" title="Return to Tomorrow">Return to Tomorrow</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Is_There_in_Truth_No_Beauty%3F" title="Is There in Truth No Beauty?">Is There in Truth No Beauty?</a>" of the original <i>Star Trek</i> series, played series regular Dr. <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Pulaski" title="Katherine Pulaski">Katherine Pulaski</a> in the second season of <i>Star Trek: The Next Generation</i>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Notable_guest_appearances">Notable guest appearances</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Notable guest appearances"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Guest roles on the series have featured actors such as:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Yvonne_Craig" title="Yvonne Craig">Yvonne Craig</a> as <a href="/wiki/Marta" class="mw-disambig" title="Marta">Marta</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Whom_Gods_Destroy_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="Whom Gods Destroy (Star Trek: The Original Series)">Whom Gods Destroy</a>"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gary_Lockwood" title="Gary Lockwood">Gary Lockwood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sally_Kellerman" title="Sally Kellerman">Sally Kellerman</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Where_No_Man_Has_Gone_Before" title="Where No Man Has Gone Before">Where No Man Has Gone Before</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Diana_Muldaur" title="Diana Muldaur">Diana Muldaur</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Return_to_Tomorrow" title="Return to Tomorrow">Return to Tomorrow</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Is_There_in_Truth_No_Beauty%3F" title="Is There in Truth No Beauty?">Is There in Truth No Beauty?</a>" (Muldaur also appeared throughout the second season of <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation" title="Star Trek: The Next Generation">Star Trek: The Next Generation</a></i> as the Enterprise-D's chief medical officer, <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Pulaski" title="Katherine Pulaski">Dr. Katherine Pulaski</a>);</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Montalb%C3%A1n" title="Ricardo Montalbán">Ricardo Montalbán</a> as <a href="/wiki/Khan_Noonien_Singh" title="Khan Noonien Singh">Khan Noonien Singh</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Space_Seed" title="Space Seed">Space Seed</a>". He then reprised the role in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_II:_The_Wrath_of_Khan" title="Star Trek II: The Wrath of Khan">Star Trek II: The Wrath of Khan</a></i>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Madlyn_Rhue" title="Madlyn Rhue">Madlyn Rhue</a> as Lieutenant Marla McGivers in "<a href="/wiki/Space_Seed" title="Space Seed">Space Seed</a>".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Ansara" title="Michael Ansara">Michael Ansara</a> as Klingon commander Kang in "<a href="/wiki/Day_of_the_Dove" title="Day of the Dove">Day of the Dove</a>", reprising the role in the <i>Deep Space Nine</i> episode "Blood Oath" and the <i>Voyager</i> episode "Flashback";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/William_Marshall_(actor)" title="William Marshall (actor)">William Marshall</a> in "<a href="/wiki/The_Ultimate_Computer" title="The Ultimate Computer">The Ultimate Computer</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Julie_Newmar" title="Julie Newmar">Julie Newmar</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Friday%27s_Child_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="Friday&#39;s Child (Star Trek: The Original Series)">Friday's Child</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kim_Darby" title="Kim Darby">Kim Darby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_J._Pollard" title="Michael J. Pollard">Michael J. Pollard</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Miri_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="Miri (Star Trek: The Original Series)">Miri</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Lansing_(actor)" title="Robert Lansing (actor)">Robert Lansing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Teri_Garr" title="Teri Garr">Teri Garr</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Assignment:_Earth" title="Assignment: Earth">Assignment: Earth</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/William_Windom_(actor)" title="William Windom (actor)">William Windom</a> in "<a href="/wiki/The_Doomsday_Machine_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="The Doomsday Machine (Star Trek: The Original Series)">The Doomsday Machine</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Colicos" title="John Colicos">John Colicos</a> as the Klingon Commander <a href="/wiki/Kor_(Star_Trek)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kor (Star Trek)">Kor</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Errand_of_Mercy" title="Errand of Mercy">Errand of Mercy</a>", reprising the role in three episodes of <i>Deep Space Nine</i>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Walker_(actor,_born_1940)" title="Robert Walker (actor, born 1940)">Robert Walker Jr.</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Charlie_X" title="Charlie X">Charlie X</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lee_Meriwether" title="Lee Meriwether">Lee Meriwether</a> in "<a href="/wiki/That_Which_Survives" title="That Which Survives">That Which Survives</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Roger_C._Carmel" title="Roger C. Carmel">Roger C. Carmel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karen_Steele" title="Karen Steele">Karen Steele</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Mudd%27s_Women" title="Mudd&#39;s Women">Mudd's Women</a>". Carmel returned in "<a href="/wiki/I,_Mudd" title="I, Mudd">I, Mudd</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/France_Nuyen" title="France Nuyen">France Nuyen</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Elaan_of_Troyius" title="Elaan of Troyius">Elaan of Troyius</a>", possibly the first Vietnamese actress to appear on American television;<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mark_Lenard" title="Mark Lenard">Mark Lenard</a>, the only actor to play members of three major non-human races in The Original Series, as the Romulan commander in "<a href="/wiki/Balance_of_Terror" title="Balance of Terror">Balance of Terror</a>", the Klingon Commander in <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Motion_Picture" title="Star Trek: The Motion Picture">Star Trek: The Motion Picture</a></i>, and most notably as Spock's father <a href="/wiki/Sarek" title="Sarek">Sarek</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Journey_to_Babel" title="Journey to Babel">Journey to Babel</a>", reprising this role in the films <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_III:_The_Search_for_Spock" title="Star Trek III: The Search for Spock">Star Trek III: The Search for Spock</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_IV:_The_Voyage_Home" title="Star Trek IV: The Voyage Home">Star Trek IV: The Voyage Home</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_VI:_The_Undiscovered_Country" title="Star Trek VI: The Undiscovered Country">Star Trek VI: The Undiscovered Country</a></i>, as well as in the <i>TNG</i> episodes "Sarek" and "Unification, Part 1";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jane_Wyatt" title="Jane Wyatt">Jane Wyatt</a> as Spock's mother Amanda Grayson in "<a href="/wiki/Journey_to_Babel" title="Journey to Babel">Journey to Babel</a>", reprising the role in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_IV:_The_Voyage_Home" title="Star Trek IV: The Voyage Home">Star Trek IV: The Voyage Home</a></i>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Glenn_Corbett" title="Glenn Corbett">Glenn Corbett</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elinor_Donahue" title="Elinor Donahue">Elinor Donahue</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Metamorphosis_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="Metamorphosis (Star Trek: The Original Series)">Metamorphosis</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elisha_Cook_Jr." title="Elisha Cook Jr.">Elisha Cook Jr.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joan_Marshall" title="Joan Marshall">Joan Marshall</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Court_Martial_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="Court Martial (Star Trek: The Original Series)">Court Martial</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nancy_Kovack" title="Nancy Kovack">Nancy Kovack</a> in "<a href="/wiki/A_Private_Little_War" title="A Private Little War">A Private Little War</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vic_Tayback" title="Vic Tayback">Vic Tayback</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Caruso_(actor)" title="Anthony Caruso (actor)">Anthony Caruso</a> in "<a href="/wiki/A_Piece_of_the_Action_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="A Piece of the Action (Star Trek: The Original Series)">A Piece of the Action</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jeff_Corey" title="Jeff Corey">Jeff Corey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fred_Williamson" title="Fred Williamson">Fred Williamson</a> in "<a href="/wiki/The_Cloud_Minders" title="The Cloud Minders">The Cloud Minders</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Barbara_Bouchet" title="Barbara Bouchet">Barbara Bouchet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warren_Stevens" title="Warren Stevens">Warren Stevens</a> in "<a href="/wiki/By_Any_Other_Name" title="By Any Other Name">By Any Other Name</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Forest" title="Michael Forest">Michael Forest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Parrish" title="Leslie Parrish">Leslie Parrish</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Who_Mourns_for_Adonais%3F" title="Who Mourns for Adonais?">Who Mourns for Adonais?</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_Napier_(actor)" title="Charles Napier (actor)">Charles Napier</a> in "<a href="/wiki/The_Way_to_Eden" title="The Way to Eden">The Way to Eden</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frank_Gorshin" title="Frank Gorshin">Frank Gorshin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lou_Antonio" title="Lou Antonio">Lou Antonio</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Let_That_Be_Your_Last_Battlefield" title="Let That Be Your Last Battlefield">Let That Be Your Last Battlefield</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ted_Cassidy" title="Ted Cassidy">Ted Cassidy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sherry_Jackson" title="Sherry Jackson">Sherry Jackson</a> in "<a href="/wiki/What_Are_Little_Girls_Made_Of%3F" title="What Are Little Girls Made Of?">What Are Little Girls Made Of?</a>"; Cassidy also voiced the Balok mannequin in <a href="/wiki/The_Corbomite_Maneuver_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Corbomite Maneuver (Star Trek: The Original Series)">The Corbomite Maneuver</a>, and the Gorn in <a href="/wiki/Arena_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="Arena (Star Trek: The Original Series)">Arena</a>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mariette_Hartley" title="Mariette Hartley">Mariette Hartley</a> in "<a href="/wiki/All_Our_Yesterdays_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="All Our Yesterdays (Star Trek: The Original Series)">All Our Yesterdays</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joan_Collins" title="Joan Collins">Joan Collins</a> in "<a href="/wiki/The_City_on_the_Edge_of_Forever" title="The City on the Edge of Forever">The City on the Edge of Forever</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Celia_Lovsky" title="Celia Lovsky">Celia Lovsky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arlene_Martel" title="Arlene Martel">Arlene Martel</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Amok_Time" title="Amok Time">Amok Time</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/David_Soul" title="David Soul">David Soul</a> in "<a href="/wiki/The_Apple_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="The Apple (Star Trek: The Original Series)">The Apple</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/James_Gregory_(actor)" title="James Gregory (actor)">James Gregory</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Dagger_of_the_Mind" title="Dagger of the Mind">Dagger of the Mind</a>";</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/James_Daly_(actor)" title="James Daly (actor)">James Daly</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Requiem_for_Methuselah" title="Requiem for Methuselah">Requiem for Methuselah</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jill_Ireland" title="Jill Ireland">Jill Ireland</a> in "<a href="/wiki/This_Side_of_Paradise_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="This Side of Paradise (Star Trek: The Original Series)">This Side of Paradise</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Melvin_Belli" title="Melvin Belli">Melvin Belli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pamelyn_Ferdin" title="Pamelyn Ferdin">Pamelyn Ferdin</a> in "<a href="/wiki/And_the_Children_Shall_Lead" title="And the Children Shall Lead">And the Children Shall Lead</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Keye_Luke" title="Keye Luke">Keye Luke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yvonne_Craig" title="Yvonne Craig">Yvonne Craig</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Ihnat" title="Steve Ihnat">Steve Ihnat</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Whom_Gods_Destroy_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="Whom Gods Destroy (Star Trek: The Original Series)">Whom Gods Destroy</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Dunn_(actor)" title="Michael Dunn (actor)">Michael Dunn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Babcock" title="Barbara Babcock">Barbara Babcock</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Plato%27s_Stepchildren" title="Plato&#39;s Stepchildren">Plato's Stepchildren</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Clint_Howard" title="Clint Howard">Clint Howard</a> in "<a href="/wiki/The_Corbomite_Maneuver" title="The Corbomite Maneuver">The Corbomite Maneuver</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/BarBara_Luna" title="BarBara Luna">Barbara Luna</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Mirror,_Mirror_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="Mirror, Mirror (Star Trek: The Original Series)">Mirror, Mirror</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/David_Opatoshu" title="David Opatoshu">David Opatoshu</a> in "<a href="/wiki/A_Taste_of_Armageddon" title="A Taste of Armageddon">A Taste of Armageddon</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Barbara_Babcock" title="Barbara Babcock">Barbara Babcock</a> in "<a href="/wiki/A_Taste_of_Armageddon" title="A Taste of Armageddon">A Taste of Armageddon</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Plato%27s_Stepchildren" title="Plato&#39;s Stepchildren">Plato's Stepchildren</a>". Her voice was also heard in "The Squire of Gothos", "Assignment: Earth", "The Tholian Web" and "The Lights of Zetar".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Morgan_Woodward" title="Morgan Woodward">Morgan Woodward</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Dagger_of_the_Mind" title="Dagger of the Mind">Dagger of the Mind</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/The_Omega_Glory" title="The Omega Glory">The Omega Glory</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arnold_Moss" title="Arnold Moss">Arnold Moss</a> as mysterious actor Anton Karidian, who proves to have originally been the tyrannical Governor Kodos of Tarsus IV in "<a href="/wiki/The_Conscience_of_the_King" title="The Conscience of the King">The Conscience of the King</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marianna_Hill" title="Marianna Hill">Marianna Hill</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Dagger_of_the_Mind" title="Dagger of the Mind">Dagger of the Mind</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joanne_Linville" title="Joanne Linville">Joanne Linville</a> in "<a href="/wiki/The_Enterprise_Incident" title="The Enterprise Incident">The Enterprise Incident</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Louise_Sorel" title="Louise Sorel">Louise Sorel</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Requiem_for_Methuselah" title="Requiem for Methuselah">Requiem for Methuselah</a>";</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Fiedler" title="John Fiedler">John Fiedler</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Wolf_in_the_Fold" title="Wolf in the Fold">Wolf in the Fold</a>;"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vic_Perrin" title="Vic Perrin">Vic Perrin</a> in "Mirror, Mirror". His voice was also heard in "The Menagerie", "Arena" and "The Changeling".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Susan_Oliver" title="Susan Oliver">Susan Oliver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Hunter" title="Jeffrey Hunter">Jeffrey Hunter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malachi_Throne" title="Malachi Throne">Malachi Throne</a> in "<a href="/wiki/The_Menagerie_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="The Menagerie (Star Trek: The Original Series)">The Menagerie</a>". Malachi Throne also voiced the main Talosian Keeper, with the voice modified so as not to be heard to be the same as the other character he played, Commodore Mendez.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Antoinette_Bower" title="Antoinette Bower">Antoinette Bower</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Catspaw_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="Catspaw (Star Trek: The Original Series)">Catspaw</a>".</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Angelique_Pettyjohn" title="Angelique Pettyjohn">Angelique Pettyjohn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Ruskin" title="Joseph Ruskin">Joseph Ruskin</a> in "<a href="/wiki/Gamesters_of_Triskelion" class="mw-redirect" title="Gamesters of Triskelion">Gamesters of Triskelion</a>".</li></ul>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Episode_analysis">Episode analysis</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Episode analysis"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Shatner_Julie_Newmar_Star_Trek_1967.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/William_Shatner_Julie_Newmar_Star_Trek_1967.jpg/250px-William_Shatner_Julie_Newmar_Star_Trek_1967.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="311" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/William_Shatner_Julie_Newmar_Star_Trek_1967.jpg/500px-William_Shatner_Julie_Newmar_Star_Trek_1967.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1619" data-file-height="2012" /></a><figcaption>Shatner and <a href="/wiki/Julie_Newmar" title="Julie Newmar">Julie Newmar</a> (1967)</figcaption></figure>
<p>In its writing, <i>Star Trek</i> is notable as one of the earliest science-fiction TV series to use the services of leading contemporary science fiction writers, such as <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bloch" title="Robert Bloch">Robert Bloch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norman_Spinrad" title="Norman Spinrad">Norman Spinrad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harlan_Ellison" title="Harlan Ellison">Harlan Ellison</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Sturgeon" title="Theodore Sturgeon">Theodore Sturgeon</a>, as well as established television writers.
</p><p>Roddenberry often used the setting of a space vessel set many years in the future to comment on social issues of 1960s America, including sexism, racism, nationalism, and global war.<sup id="cite_ref-page19680815_50-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page19680815-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In November 1968, just a few months after the <a href="/wiki/Petula_Clark#International_fame_–_the_&quot;Downtown&quot;_era" title="Petula Clark">first televised interracial touch</a>, the episode "<a href="/wiki/Plato%27s_Stepchildren" title="Plato&#39;s Stepchildren">Plato's Stepchildren</a>" went <a href="/wiki/First_interracial_kiss_on_television#Star_Trek" title="First interracial kiss on television">incorrectly</a><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> down in history as the first American television show to feature a scripted interracial kiss between characters (Capt. Kirk and Lt. Uhura), although the kiss was only mimed (obscured by the back of a character's head) and depicted as involuntary.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There is however some dispute to this being the first interracial kiss of the series because the 1967 episode "<a href="/wiki/Space_Seed" title="Space Seed">Space Seed</a>" – introducing the villain <a href="/wiki/Khan_Noonien_Singh" title="Khan Noonien Singh">Khan</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Montalb%C3%A1n" title="Ricardo Montalbán">Ricardo Montalbán</a>) – has him seducing and kissing Lt. Marla McGivers (<a href="/wiki/Madlyn_Rhue" title="Madlyn Rhue">Madlyn Rhue</a>) as part of his malicious machinations. "<a href="/wiki/Let_That_Be_Your_Last_Battlefield" title="Let That Be Your Last Battlefield">Let That Be Your Last Battlefield</a>" presented a direct allegory about the irrationality and futility of racism. Anti-war themes appear in episodes such as "<a href="/wiki/The_Doomsday_Machine_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="The Doomsday Machine (Star Trek: The Original Series)">The Doomsday Machine</a>", depicting a planet-destroying weapon as an analogy to nuclear weapons deployed under the principle of <a href="/wiki/Mutually_assured_destruction" class="mw-redirect" title="Mutually assured destruction">mutually assured destruction</a>, and "<a href="/wiki/A_Taste_of_Armageddon" title="A Taste of Armageddon">A Taste of Armageddon</a>" about a society which has "civilized" war to the point that they no longer see it as something to avoid.
</p><p>Episodes such as "<a href="/wiki/The_Apple_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="The Apple (Star Trek: The Original Series)">The Apple</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Who_Mourns_for_Adonais%3F" title="Who Mourns for Adonais?">Who Mourns for Adonais?</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Mark_of_Gideon" title="The Mark of Gideon">The Mark of Gideon</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/The_Return_of_the_Archons" title="The Return of the Archons">The Return of the Archons</a>" display subtle anti-religious (owing mainly to Roddenberry's own <a href="/wiki/Secular_humanism" title="Secular humanism">secular humanism</a>) and anti-establishment themes. "<a href="/wiki/Bread_and_Circuses_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="Bread and Circuses (Star Trek: The Original Series)">Bread and Circuses</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/The_Omega_Glory" title="The Omega Glory">The Omega Glory</a>" have themes that are more pro-Christian or patriotic.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (January 2012)">original research?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The show experienced network and/or sponsor interference, up to and including wholesale censorship of scripts and film footage. This was a regular occurrence in the 1960s and <i>Star Trek</i> suffered from its fair share of tampering. Scripts were routinely vetted and censored by the staff of NBC's Broadcast Standards Department, which copiously annotated every script with demands for cuts or changes (e.g. "Page 4: Please delete McCoy's expletive, 'Good Lord<span style="padding-right:.15em;">'</span>" or "Page 43: Caution on the embrace; avoid open-mouthed kiss").<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The series was noted for its sense of humor, such as Spock and McCoy's pointed, yet friendly, bickering. Certain episodes, such as "<a href="/wiki/The_Trouble_with_Tribbles" title="The Trouble with Tribbles">The Trouble with Tribbles</a>", "<a href="/wiki/I,_Mudd" title="I, Mudd">I, Mudd</a>" and <a href="/wiki/A_Piece_of_the_Action_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="A Piece of the Action (Star Trek: The Original Series)">"A Piece of the Action"</a>, were written and staged as comedies with dramatic elements. Most episodes were presented as action/adventure dramas, frequently including space battles or fist fights between the ship's crew and guest antagonists.
</p><p>Several episodes used the concept of planets developing parallel to Earth, allowing reuse of stock props, costumes and sets. "Bread and Circuses", "<a href="/wiki/Miri_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="Miri (Star Trek: The Original Series)">Miri</a>" and "The Omega Glory" depict such worlds; "A Piece of the Action", <a href="/wiki/Patterns_of_Force_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="Patterns of Force (Star Trek: The Original Series)">"Patterns of Force"</a> and "Plato's Stepchildren" are based on alien planets that have adopted period Earth cultures (Prohibition-era Chicago, Nazi Germany and ancient Greece, respectively). Two episodes depicting time travel ("<a href="/wiki/Tomorrow_Is_Yesterday" title="Tomorrow Is Yesterday">Tomorrow Is Yesterday</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Assignment:_Earth" title="Assignment: Earth">Assignment: Earth</a>") conveniently place <i>Enterprise</i> in orbit above 1960s Earth; a third ("<a href="/wiki/The_City_on_the_Edge_of_Forever" title="The City on the Edge of Forever">The City on the Edge of Forever</a>") places members of the crew on 1930s Earth.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Top_ranked_episodes">Top ranked episodes</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Top ranked episodes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

<td>"<span data-sort-value="enter&#160;!">The Enterprise Incident</span>"
</td>
<td>"<a href="/wiki/The_Man_Trap" title="The Man Trap">The Man Trap</a>"
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Of the twenty-one different episodes listed above, thirteen – "Where No Man Has Gone Before", "The Enemy Within", "The Naked Time", "Balance of Terror", "The Galileo Seven", "Arena", "Space Seed", "This Side of Paradise", "The Devil in the Dark", "A Taste of Armageddon", "The Corbomite Maneuver", "The Man Trap", and "The City on the Edge of Forever" – are from the first season and six – "Amok Time", "The Doomsday Machine", "Mirror, Mirror", "The Trouble with Tribbles", "A Piece of the Action", and "Journey to Babel" – are from the second season. Only two – "The Enterprise Incident" and "Let That Be Your Last Battlefield" – derive from the third season.
</p><p>Only two episodes, "The City on the Edge of Forever" and "Space Seed", appear on all five lists.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Leonard_Nimoy:_Star_Trek_Memories"><i>Leonard Nimoy: Star Trek Memories</i></h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Leonard Nimoy: Star Trek Memories"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 1983, Leonard Nimoy hosted a one-hour special as a promotional tie-in with the film <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_III:_The_Search_for_Spock" title="Star Trek III: The Search for Spock">Star Trek III: The Search for Spock</a></i>, in which he recounted his memories of working on the original series and explained the origins of things such as the <a href="/wiki/Vulcan_nerve_pinch" title="Vulcan nerve pinch">Vulcan nerve pinch</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vulcan_salute" title="Vulcan salute">Vulcan salute</a>, as well as a re-airing of the TOS episode "<a href="/wiki/Space_Seed" title="Space Seed">Space Seed</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Music">Music</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Music"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Theme_tune">Theme tune</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Theme tune"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Theme_from_Star_Trek" title="Theme from Star Trek">Theme from Star Trek</a></div>
<p>The show's theme tune was written by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Courage" title="Alexander Courage">Alexander Courage</a> and has been featured in several <i>Star Trek</i> spin-off episodes and motion pictures. Gene Roddenberry subsequently wrote a set of accompanying lyrics, even though the lyrics were never used in the series, nor did Roddenberry ever intend them to be; this allowed him to claim co-composer credit and hence 50% of the theme's performance royalties. Courage considered Roddenberry's actions, while entirely legal, to be unethical.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Series producer <a href="/wiki/Robert_H._Justman" title="Robert H. Justman">Robert Justman</a> noted in the book <i>Inside Star Trek: The Real Story</i>, that work on the film <i><a href="/wiki/Doctor_Dolittle_(1967_film)" title="Doctor Dolittle (1967 film)">Doctor Dolittle</a></i> kept Courage from working on more than two episodes of the first season. However, Justman also believed that Courage lost enthusiasm for the series because of the "royalty" issue.<sup id="cite_ref-solow1997_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solow1997-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 185">&#58;&#8202;185&#8202;</span></sup> Courage did not score any episodes of the second season; however, he did conduct a recording session for about 30 minutes of "library cues" for the second season, on June 16, 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-BondLiner_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BondLiner-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Courage returned to score two episodes of the third season.
</p><p>Later episodes used stock recordings from Courage's earlier work. Jazz trumpeter <a href="/wiki/Maynard_Ferguson" title="Maynard Ferguson">Maynard Ferguson</a> recorded a <a href="/wiki/Jazz_fusion" title="Jazz fusion">jazz fusion</a> version of the tune with his band during the late 1970s, and Nichelle Nichols performed the song live complete with lyrics.
</p><p>The lyrics for the song are:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1244412712" /><blockquote class="templatequote"><div class="poem">
<p>Beyond the rim of the starlight<br />
My love is wandering in star flight<br />
I know he'll find<br />
In star clustered reaches<br />
Love, strange love<br />
A starwoman teaches<br />
<br />
I know his journey ends never<br />
His Star Trek will go on forever<br />
But tell him while<br />
He wanders his starry sea<br />
Remember<br />
Remember me<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
</div></blockquote>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Dramatic_underscore">Dramatic underscore</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Dramatic underscore"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>For budgetary reasons, this series made significant use of "tracked" music, or music written for other episodes that was reused in later episodes. Of the 79 episodes that were broadcast, only 31 had complete or partial original dramatic underscores created specifically for them. The remainder of the music in any episode was tracked from other episodes and from cues recorded for the music library. Which episodes would have new music was mostly the decision of Robert H. Justman, the Associate Producer during the first two seasons.
</p><p>Screen credits for the composers were given based on the amount of music composed for, or composed and reused in, the episode. Some of these final music credits were occasionally incorrect.
</p><p>Beyond the short works of <a href="/wiki/Source_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Source music">"source" music</a> (music whose source is seen or acknowledged onscreen) created for specific episodes, eight composers were contracted to create original dramatic underscore during the series run: <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Courage" title="Alexander Courage">Alexander Courage</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Duning" title="George Duning">George Duning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Fielding" title="Jerry Fielding">Jerry Fielding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Fried" title="Gerald Fried">Gerald Fried</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sol_Kaplan" title="Sol Kaplan">Sol Kaplan</a>, Samuel Matlovsky, Joseph Mullendore, and <a href="/wiki/Fred_Steiner" title="Fred Steiner">Fred Steiner</a>. The composers conducted their own music. Of these composers, Steiner composed the original music for thirteen episodes and it is his instrumental arrangement of Alexander Courage's main theme that is heard over many of the end title credits of the series.
</p><p>The tracked musical underscores were chosen and edited to the episode by the music editors, principal of whom were Robert Raff (most of Season One), Jim Henrikson (Season One and Two), and Richard Lapham (Season Three).<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Some of the original recordings of the music were released in the United States commercially on the <a href="/wiki/GNP_Crescendo_Record_Co." class="mw-redirect" title="GNP Crescendo Record Co.">GNP Crescendo Record Co.</a> label. Music for a number of the episodes was re-recorded by <a href="/wiki/Fred_Steiner" title="Fred Steiner">Fred Steiner</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Royal Philharmonic Orchestra">Royal Philharmonic Orchestra</a> for the <i><a href="/wiki/Var%C3%A8se_Sarabande" title="Varèse Sarabande">Varèse Sarabande</a></i> label; and by Tony Bremner with the Royal Philharmonic for the <i>Label X</i> label. Finally in December 2012, the complete original recordings were released by La-La Land Records as a 15-CD <a href="/wiki/Box_set#Music_box_sets" title="Box set">box set</a>, with liner notes by Jeff Bond.<sup id="cite_ref-Lalaland_TOS_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lalaland_TOS-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Episodes_with_original_music">Episodes with original music</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Episodes with original music"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Listed in production order. Episodes that were only partially scored are in italics.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><i>Season 1</i>:

"Requiem for Methuselah" contains a <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Brahms" title="Johannes Brahms">Johannes Brahms</a> interpretation by Ivan Ditmars.

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Awards">Awards</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Awards"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series" title="List of awards and nominations received by Star Trek: The Original Series">List of awards and nominations received by Star Trek: The Original Series</a></div>
<p>Although this series never won any Emmys, <i>Star Trek</i> was nominated for the following <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Awards</a>:
</p>
<ul><li>Outstanding Dramatic Series (Gene Roddenberry and <a href="/wiki/Gene_L._Coon" title="Gene L. Coon">Gene L. Coon</a>), 1967</li>
<li>Outstanding Dramatic Series (Gene Roddenberry), 1968</li>
<li>Outstanding Supporting Actor (<a href="/wiki/Leonard_Nimoy" title="Leonard Nimoy">Leonard Nimoy</a> as Mr. Spock), 1967, 1968, 1969</li>
<li>Individual Achievement in Art Direction and Allied Crafts (Jim Rugg), 1967</li>
<li>Individual Achievement in Cinematography (Darrell Anderson, Linwood G. Dunn, and Joseph Westheimer), 1967</li>
<li>Individual Achievement in Film and Sound Editing (<a href="/wiki/Doug_Grindstaff" title="Doug Grindstaff">Doug Grindstaff</a>), 1967</li>
<li>Outstanding Achievement in Film Editing (Donald R. Rode), 1968</li>
<li>Special Classification of Individual Achievement for Photographic Effects (The Westheimer Company), 1968</li>
<li>Outstanding Achievement in Art Direction and Scenic Design (John Dwyer and Walter M. Jefferies), 1969</li>
<li>Outstanding Achievement in Film Editing (Donald R. Rode), 1969</li>
<li>Special Classification Achievements for Photographic Effects (The Howard A. Anderson Company, The Westheimer Company, <a href="/wiki/Van_der_Veer_Photo_Effects" class="mw-redirect" title="Van der Veer Photo Effects">Van der Veer Photo Effects</a>, Cinema Research), 1969.</li></ul>
<p>Eight of its episodes were nominated for one of science-fiction's top awards, the <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Award" title="Hugo Award">Hugo Award</a>, in the category "Best Dramatic Presentation". In 1967, the nominated episodes were "<a href="/wiki/The_Naked_Time" title="The Naked Time">The Naked Time</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Corbomite_Maneuver" title="The Corbomite Maneuver">The Corbomite Maneuver</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/The_Menagerie_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="The Menagerie (Star Trek: The Original Series)">The Menagerie</a>". In 1968, all nominees were <i>Star Trek</i> episodes: "<a href="/wiki/Amok_Time" title="Amok Time">Amok Time</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Mirror,_Mirror_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="Mirror, Mirror (Star Trek: The Original Series)">Mirror, Mirror</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Doomsday_Machine_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="The Doomsday Machine (Star Trek: The Original Series)">The Doomsday Machine</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Trouble_with_Tribbles" title="The Trouble with Tribbles">The Trouble with Tribbles</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/The_City_on_the_Edge_of_Forever" title="The City on the Edge of Forever">The City on the Edge of Forever</a>". <i>Star Trek</i> won both years for the episodes "The Menagerie" and "The City on the Edge of Forever", respectively. In 1968, <i>Star Trek</i> won a special <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Award" title="Hugo Award">Hugo Award</a> for Dramatic Presentation. No episode was named. This was the show's 3rd <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Award" title="Hugo Award">Hugo Award</a>, and 9th Hugo nomination.
</p><p>In 1967, <i>Star Trek</i> was also one of the first television programs to receive an <a href="/wiki/NAACP_Image_Awards" title="NAACP Image Awards">NAACP Image Award</a>. 
</p><p>In 1968, <i>Star Trek</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s most critically acclaimed episode, "The City on the Edge of Forever", written by <a href="/wiki/Harlan_Ellison" title="Harlan Ellison">Harlan Ellison</a>, won the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Writers_Guild_of_America_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Writers Guild of America Award">Writers Guild of America Award</a> for Best Original Teleplay, although this was for Ellison's original draft script, and not for the screenplay of the episode as it aired.
</p><p>In 1997, "The City on the Edge of Forever" was ranked #92 on <a href="/wiki/TV_Guide%27s_100_Greatest_Episodes_of_All_Time" title="TV Guide&#39;s 100 Greatest Episodes of All Time"><i>TV Guide</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s 100 Greatest Episodes of All Time</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004 and 2007, <i><a href="/wiki/TV_Guide" title="TV Guide">TV Guide</a></i> ranked <i>Star Trek</i> as the greatest cult show ever.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, <i>TV Guide</i> ranked <i>Star Trek</i> as the greatest sci-fi show (along with <i>Star Trek: The Next Generation</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the #12 greatest show of all time,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/Writers_Guild_of_America" title="Writers Guild of America">Writers Guild of America</a> ranked it #33 on their list of the 101 Best Written TV Series.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Distribution">Distribution</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Distribution"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Home_media">Home media</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Home media"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Episodes of the <i>Original Series</i> were among the first television series to be released on the VHS and <a href="/wiki/Laserdisc" class="mw-redirect" title="Laserdisc">laserdisc</a> formats in North America. The first episode on VHS for sale to the public was <i><a href="/wiki/Space_Seed" title="Space Seed">Space Seed</a></i> released in June 1982 (to celebrate the release of the second Star Trek film, The Wrath of Khan) at a price of $29.95, as prior to this titles were rental only.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1985, the first 10 episodes went on sale on video at a price of $14.95 with further batches of 10 during 1985 and 1986, making it the first long-running TV series to be released on <a href="/wiki/Home_video" title="Home video">home video</a> in its entirety,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> with all episodes eventually being released on both formats. By 1986, sales had reached 1&#160;million units.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> With the advent of DVD in the mid-1990s, single DVDs featuring two episodes each in production order were released. In the early 2000s, Paramount Home Video reissued the series to DVD in a series of three deluxe season boxes with added featurettes and documentaries. In February 2009 CBS and Paramount announced that they would release the Original Series on Blu-ray. Season one, two, and three were released on April 28, September 22, and December 15, respectively. The Blu-ray releases let the user choose between "Enhanced Effects" or "Original Effects" via a technique called <a href="/wiki/Multi-angle" class="mw-redirect" title="Multi-angle">multi-angle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>All 79 episodes of the series have been digitally remastered by <a href="/wiki/CBS_Home_Entertainment" title="CBS Home Entertainment">CBS Home Entertainment</a> (distributed by <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">Paramount</a>) and have since been released on DVD.
CBS Home Entertainment released season one of <i>The Original Series</i> on Blu-ray on April 28, 2009. The Blu-ray release contains both Original and Remastered episodes by <a href="/wiki/Seamless_branching" title="Seamless branching">seamless branching</a>.
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Online_distribution">Online distribution</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Online distribution"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/CBS_Interactive" class="mw-redirect" title="CBS Interactive">CBS Interactive</a> is presenting all 3 seasons of the series via the <a href="/wiki/Tv.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Tv.com">tv.com</a> <a href="/wiki/IPhone_app" class="mw-redirect" title="IPhone app">iPhone app</a>. The full-length episodes, without the new CGI but digitally processed to remove the original celluloid artifacts, are available to users in the US at no charge but with embedded ads. Short clips from the shows are also viewable at their web site.<sup id="cite_ref-waldman_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waldman-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
The company has recently presented all 3 seasons of the series via its <a href="/wiki/Paramount%2B" title="Paramount+">Paramount+</a> premium streaming service. It has all full-length episodes, without the new CGI, like the tv.com app, and is available to users in the US with subscription without ad interruptions.
</p><p>In January 2007, the first season of <i>Star Trek: The Original Series</i> became available for download from <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>'s <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a>. Although consumer reviews indicate that some of the episodes on iTunes are the newly "remastered" editions, iTunes editors had not indicated such, and if so, which are which. All first-season episodes that had been remastered and aired were available from iTunes, except "<a href="/wiki/Where_No_Man_Has_Gone_Before" title="Where No Man Has Gone Before">Where No Man Has Gone Before</a>", which remains in its original form. On March 20, 2007, the first season was again added to the iTunes Store, with separate downloads for the original and remastered versions of the show, though according to the customer reviews, the original version contains minor revisions such as special effect enhancements.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> began online streaming of five of the six <i>Star Trek</i> television series on July 1, 2011; <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Deep_Space_Nine" title="Star Trek: Deep Space Nine">Deep Space Nine</a></i> followed on October 1, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Films">Films</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Films"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><b><i>The Original Series</i> films</b>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_(film_series)#The_Original_Series_films" class="mw-redirect" title="Star Trek (film series)">Star Trek (film series) §&#160;The Original Series films</a></div>
<p><i>Star Trek</i> creator Gene Roddenberry first suggested the idea of a <i>Star Trek</i> feature in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-reeves-stevens_155_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reeves-stevens_155-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> When the original television series was canceled, he lobbied to continue the franchise through a film. The success of the series in <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_syndication" title="Broadcast syndication">syndication</a> convinced the studio to begin work on a feature film in 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-Locus180_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Locus180-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A series of writers attempted to craft a suitably epic screenplay, but the attempts did not satisfy Paramount, so the studio scrapped the project in 1977. Paramount instead planned on returning the franchise to its roots with a new television series (<i>Phase II</i>). The massive worldwide box office success of <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_(film)" title="Star Wars (film)">Star Wars</a></i> in mid-1977 sent Hollywood studios to their vaults in search of similar sci-fi properties that could be adapted or re-launched to the big screen. Following the huge opening of <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Pictures" title="Columbia Pictures">Columbia</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Close_Encounters_of_the_Third_Kind" title="Close Encounters of the Third Kind">Close Encounters of the Third Kind</a></i> in late December 1977, production of <i>Phase II</i> was canceled in favor of making a <i>Star Trek</i> film.<sup id="cite_ref-SyFyWire-20170927_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SyFyWire-20170927-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Beginning with <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Motion_Picture" title="Star Trek: The Motion Picture">Star Trek: The Motion Picture</a></i> in 1979, it was followed by five sequels, <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_II:_The_Wrath_of_Khan" title="Star Trek II: The Wrath of Khan">Star Trek II: The Wrath of Khan</a></i> (1982), <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_III:_The_Search_for_Spock" title="Star Trek III: The Search for Spock">Star Trek III: The Search for Spock</a></i> (1984), <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_IV:_The_Voyage_Home" title="Star Trek IV: The Voyage Home">Star Trek IV: The Voyage Home</a></i> (1986), <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_V:_The_Final_Frontier" title="Star Trek V: The Final Frontier">Star Trek V: The Final Frontier</a></i> (1989) and <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_VI:_The_Undiscovered_Country" title="Star Trek VI: The Undiscovered Country">Star Trek VI: The Undiscovered Country</a></i> (1991). Leonard Nimoy directed <i>Star Trek</i>s III and IV, while William Shatner directed <i>Star Trek</i> V.
</p><p><b>Reboot films (The Kelvin Timeline)</b>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_(film_series)#The_Kelvin_Timeline" class="mw-redirect" title="Star Trek (film series)">Star Trek (film series) §&#160;The Kelvin Timeline</a></div>
<p>After the poor reception of the final <i>Next Generation</i> film <i>Nemesis</i> and the cancellation of the television series <i>Enterprise</i>, the franchise's executive producer <a href="/wiki/Rick_Berman" title="Rick Berman">Rick Berman</a> and screenwriter <a href="/wiki/Erik_Jendresen" title="Erik Jendresen">Erik Jendresen</a> began developing a new film,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> titled <i>Star Trek: The Beginning</i>, which would take place after <i>Enterprise</i> but before <i>The Original Series</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In February 2007, <a href="/wiki/J._J._Abrams" title="J. J. Abrams">J. J. Abrams</a> accepted Paramount's offer to direct the new film, having been previously attached as producer.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Orci" title="Roberto Orci">Roberto Orci</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alex_Kurtzman" title="Alex Kurtzman">Alex Kurtzman</a> wrote a screenplay that impressed Abrams, featuring new actors portraying younger versions of the original series' cast. The <i>Enterprise</i>, its interior, and the original uniforms were redesigned.
</p><p>This revival of the franchise is often considered to be a <a href="/wiki/Reboot_(fiction)" title="Reboot (fiction)">reboot</a>, but is also a continuation of the franchise, with Nimoy reprising his role of the elderly Spock. This route was taken to free the new films from the restrictions of established continuity without completely discarding it, which the writers felt would have been "disrespectful". This new reality was informally referred to by several names, including the "Abramsverse", "JJ Trek" and "NuTrek", before it was named the "Kelvin Timeline" (versus the "Prime Timeline" of the original series and films) by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Okuda" title="Michael Okuda">Michael</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denise_Okuda" title="Denise Okuda">Denise Okuda</a> for use in official <i>Star Trek</i> reference guides and encyclopedias. The name Kelvin comes from USS <i>Kelvin</i>, a starship involved in the event that creates the new reality in <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_(2009_film)" title="Star Trek (2009 film)">Star Trek</a></i> (2009).<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Abrams named the starship after his grandfather Henry Kelvin, whom he also pays tribute to in <i>Into Darkness</i> with the Kelvin Memorial Archive.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>The three films in the Kelvin Timeline include <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_(2009_film)" title="Star Trek (2009 film)">Star Trek</a></i> (2009), <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_Into_Darkness" title="Star Trek Into Darkness">Star Trek Into Darkness</a></i> (2013) and <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_Beyond" title="Star Trek Beyond">Star Trek Beyond</a></i> (2016). The last was dedicated to Nimoy, who died in 2015 and <a href="/wiki/Anton_Yelchin" title="Anton Yelchin">Anton Yelchin</a>, who died in a <a href="/wiki/Car_crash" class="mw-redirect" title="Car crash">car crash</a> in the summer it was released.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Merchandising">Merchandising</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Merchandising"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
