<p><i>Star Trek: The Original Series</i> has inspired many commercial products, including toys, comic books, and many other materials. The comics are generally considered <a href="/wiki/Non-canonical" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-canonical">non-canonical</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Action_figures">Action figures</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Action figures"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In the early 1970s the <a href="/wiki/Mego_Corporation" title="Mego Corporation">Mego Corporation</a> acquired the license to produce <i>Star Trek</i> <a href="/wiki/Action_figure" title="Action figure">action figures</a>, which the company successfully marketed from 1974 to 1976. During this period, the company produced a line of 8" figures featuring <a href="/wiki/James_T._Kirk" title="James T. Kirk">Captain Kirk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mr._Spock" class="mw-redirect" title="Mr. Spock">Mr. Spock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leonard_McCoy" title="Leonard McCoy">Leonard McCoy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mr._Scott" class="mw-redirect" title="Mr. Scott">Mr. Scott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lt._Uhura" class="mw-redirect" title="Lt. Uhura">Lt. Uhura</a>, "Aliens" (a <a href="/wiki/Klingon" title="Klingon">Klingon</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Neptunian" class="mw-redirect" title="Neptunian">Neptunian</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Cage_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="The Cage (Star Trek: The Original Series)">the Keeper</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Gorn" title="Gorn">Gorn</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Let_That_Be_Your_Last_Battlefield" title="Let That Be Your Last Battlefield">Cheron</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Romulan" title="Romulan">Romulan</a>, a <a href="/wiki/The_Cage_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="The Cage (Star Trek: The Original Series)">Talosian</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Andorian" title="Andorian">Andorian</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Mugato" class="mw-redirect" title="Mugato">Mugato</a>), and numerous playsets. (Mego also produced a "life-size" toy <a href="/wiki/Tricorder" title="Tricorder">tricorder</a>.)
</p><p>In the mid-2000s, Paul "Dr. Mego" Clarke and Joe Sena founded EMCE Toys (pronounced "MC") to bring Mego toys back to the marketplace. (Mego went out of business in 1983.)<sup id="cite_ref-Caringer_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caringer-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Working with <a href="/wiki/Diamond_Select_Toys" title="Diamond Select Toys">Diamond Select Toys</a>, current holders of the <i>Star Trek</i> license, these figures have been selling in comics shops. New characters are currently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (December 2014)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> being produced that Mego did not originally make, such as <a href="/wiki/Hikaru_Sulu" title="Hikaru Sulu">Lt. Sulu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Chekov" title="Pavel Chekov">Ensign Chekov</a>, and "<a href="/wiki/Space_Seed" title="Space Seed">Space Seed</a>" villain <a href="/wiki/Khan_Noonien_Singh" title="Khan Noonien Singh">Khan Noonien Singh</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Gorn" title="Gorn">Gorn</a> that Mego produced had a brown <a href="/wiki/Lizard_(character)" title="Lizard (character)">Lizard</a> head (identical to the Marvel Comics villain) on a brown body wearing a <a href="/wiki/Klingon" title="Klingon">Klingon</a> outfit. <i>Star Trek</i> fans had frequently wished that Mego had made a "TV-accurate" Gorn; EMCE Toys and DST produced a new green Gorn based on the TV episode "<a href="/wiki/Arena_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="Arena (Star Trek: The Original Series)">Arena</a>".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> EMCE Toys hired original Mego packaging artist Harold Schull to illustrate new artwork for Sulu, Chekov, Khan, and the Gorn.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> EMCE Toys is continuing the Mego revival with the production of more <i>Star Trek</i> figures, including <a href="/wiki/Captain_Pike" class="mw-redirect" title="Captain Pike">Captain Pike</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Salt_Vampire" class="mw-redirect" title="Salt Vampire">Salt Vampire</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Comic_books">Comic books</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Comic books"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_(comics)" title="Star Trek (comics)">Star Trek (comics)</a></div>
<p>The first <i>Star Trek</i> comics were published by <a href="/wiki/Gold_Key_Comics" title="Gold Key Comics">Gold Key Comics</a> between 1967 and 1978. These comics were highly stylized and diverged wildly from the TV series continuity. Most storylines used in the Gold Key series featured original characters and concepts, although later issues did include sequels to the original series episodes "<a href="/wiki/The_City_on_the_Edge_of_Forever_(TOS_episode)" class="mw-redirect" title="The City on the Edge of Forever (TOS episode)">The City on the Edge of Forever</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Metamorphosis_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="Metamorphosis (Star Trek: The Original Series)">Metamorphosis</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/I,_Mudd" title="I, Mudd">I, Mudd</a>". Writers included George Kashdan, <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Drake" title="Arnold Drake">Arnold Drake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Len_Wein" title="Len Wein">Len Wein</a>. Originally they were illustrated by <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Giolitti" title="Alberto Giolitti">Alberto Giolitti</a>, an Italian artist who had never seen the series and only had publicity photos to use as references. Since Giolitti didn't have a publicity photo of <a href="/wiki/James_Doohan" title="James Doohan">James Doohan</a>, early issues of the series had Mr. Scott drawn differently. The original issues, most of which featured photographic covers showing images from the series, are highly collectable. They are fondly remembered by fans, and a series of reprints ("The Key Collection") of these original titles began to appear in 2004, published by Checker. The Gold Key series had a run of 61 issues. Gold Key lost the <i>Star Trek</i> license to <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Comics" title="Marvel Comics">Marvel Comics</a> in 1979 (although Marvel's license from Paramount prohibited them from utilizing concepts introduced in the original series).<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>From 1969 to 1973, a series of weekly <i>Star Trek</i> <a href="/wiki/Comic_strip" title="Comic strip">comic strips</a> ran in the British comics magazine eventually known as <i><a href="/wiki/TV_Century_21" title="TV Century 21">TV Century 21</a></i>. A total of 258 issues were produced, as well as various annuals and specials. All were original stories. Two more annuals, under the <i>Mighty TV Comic</i> banner, also produced original <i>Star Trek</i> materials. In addition, the weekly <i><a href="/wiki/TV_Comic" title="TV Comic">TV Comic</a></i> reprinted serialized versions of the U.S. Gold Key comics.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 1977–1978, before <a href="/wiki/Home_video" title="Home video">home video</a> was widely available, Mandala Productions and <a href="/wiki/Bantam_Books" title="Bantam Books">Bantam Books</a> published <a href="/wiki/Photonovel" class="mw-redirect" title="Photonovel">FotoNovels</a> of <i>TOS</i> that included direct adaptations of actual color television episode frames (with <a href="/wiki/Word_balloons" class="mw-redirect" title="Word balloons">word balloons</a>) in comics format.
</p><p>From February 1984 through February 1996, <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">DC Comics</a> held the license to publish comic books based upon the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek" title="Star Trek">Star Trek</a></i> franchise, including <i>Star Trek: The Original Series</i>. The main DC Comics <i>Star Trek</i> title was published in two series, comprising 136 issues, 9 annuals, and a number of special issues, plus several mini-series that linked <i>TOS</i> and the subsequent series <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation" title="Star Trek: The Next Generation">Star Trek: The Next Generation</a></i> (<i>TNG</i>).
</p><p>Marvel Comics again obtained the <i>Star Trek</i> license in 1996. Marvel (under the "Marvel/Paramount comics" imprint) published various one-shots and the quarterly <i>Star Trek Unlimited</i> series, which covered <i>TOS</i> as well as <i>TNG</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They also introduced the new series <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Early_Voyages" title="Star Trek: Early Voyages">Star Trek: Early Voyages</a></i>, which dealt with <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Pike_(Star_Trek)" title="Christopher Pike (Star Trek)">Christopher Pike</a>'s adventures as captain of the <i>Enterprise</i> (as depicted in the rejected <i>TOS</i> pilot "<a href="/wiki/The_Cage_(Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series)" title="The Cage (Star Trek: The Original Series)">The Cage</a>"). Fan acceptance of these comics got off to a shaky start when Marvel's inaugural publication of its new <i>Star Trek</i> line turned out to be a crossover between <i>TOS</i> and Marvel's popular superhero team, the <a href="/wiki/X-Men" title="X-Men">X-Men</a>. However, the series turned out to be relatively popular, registering strong sales.
</p><p>Beginning in 2006, <a href="/wiki/Tokyopop" title="Tokyopop">Tokyopop</a> published two projects based upon the original series. The new comic anthologies, produced by <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Ortega" title="Joshua Ortega">Joshua Ortega</a>, were released annually in September 2006 (<i>Shinsei Shinsei</i>) and 2007 (<i>Kakan ni Shinkou</i>). Five artists and writer teams presented five new stories, per volume, based on the original series.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Legacy_and_cultural_influence">Legacy and cultural influence</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Legacy and cultural influence"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cultural_influence_of_Star_Trek" title="Cultural influence of Star Trek">Cultural influence of Star Trek</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Parodies">Parodies</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Parodies"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><i>The Original Series</i> has been parodied many times in other television series. <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i> produced two famous sketches parodying <i>The Original Series</i>, <a href="/wiki/The_Last_Voyage_of_the_Starship_Enterprise" title="The Last Voyage of the Starship Enterprise">"The Last Voyage of the Starship <i>Enterprise</i>"</a> in 1976<sup id="cite_ref-LVSE_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LVSE-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and William Shatner's own "<a href="/wiki/Get_a_life_(idiom)" title="Get a life (idiom)">Get a life</a>" sketch in 1986 (which parodied the show's "trekkie" followers). "The Last Voyage of the Starship <i>Enterprise</i>" is a twelve-minute sketch, written by <a href="/wiki/Michael_O%27Donoghue" title="Michael O&#39;Donoghue">Michael O'Donoghue</a>. It was described by <a href="/wiki/TrekMovie.com" title="TrekMovie.com">TrekMovie.com</a> as "one of the best <i>Star Trek</i> parody sketches of all time".<sup id="cite_ref-LVSE_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LVSE-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/TVSquad" class="mw-redirect" title="TVSquad">TVSquad</a> ranked Shatner's "Get a life" sketch alongside "The Last Voyage<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>..." as one of the most famous parodies of the show.<sup id="cite_ref-TVS_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TVS-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Canadian comedy duo <a href="/wiki/Wayne_and_Shuster" title="Wayne and Shuster">Wayne and Shuster</a> parodied <i>Star Trek</i> as <i>Star Schtick</i> in the late 1970s. An entire Finnish parody series <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wreck" title="Star Wreck">Star Wreck</a></i> was produced starting in 1992, culminating with <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wreck:_In_the_Pirkinning" title="Star Wreck: In the Pirkinning">Star Wreck: In the Pirkinning</a></i> in 2005, all available as legal downloads on the web.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The series has also been parodied on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-TVS_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TVS-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Family_Guy" title="Family Guy">Family Guy</a></i> and notably in the <i><a href="/wiki/Futurama" title="Futurama">Futurama</a></i> episode "<a href="/wiki/Where_No_Fan_Has_Gone_Before" title="Where No Fan Has Gone Before">Where No Fan Has Gone Before</a>", which was described by <a href="/wiki/Wired_(magazine)" title="Wired (magazine)"><i>Wired</i> magazine</a> as a "touchstone" for fans.<sup id="cite_ref-GameLife_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GameLife-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The 1999 film <i><a href="/wiki/Galaxy_Quest" title="Galaxy Quest">Galaxy Quest</a></i> portrays the lives of a once-popular television space-drama crew who are kidnapped by real aliens who have mistaken the fictional series for reality.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The main characters are parodies of <i>Star Trek</i> characters, and many of the plot elements refer to or parody popular 1960s TV-series customs.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Adult_Swim" title="Adult Swim">Adult Swim</a><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s <i><a href="/wiki/FishCenter_Live" title="FishCenter Live">FishCenter Live</a></i>, a parody of the <a href="/wiki/USS_Enterprise_(NCC-1701)" title="USS Enterprise (NCC-1701)">USS <i>Enterprise</i></a> was featured called the "USS <i>FishCenterprise</i> NCC-1065".<sup id="cite_ref-Hillebrand_&amp;_Schneider_2020_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hillebrand_&amp;_Schneider_2020-151"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The series was also parodied in print as "Star Blecch" in the December 1967 issue of Mad Magazine (Issue #115).<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>John Scalzi's novel <i>Redshirts</i>, winner of the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Award" title="Hugo Award">Hugo Award</a> for Best Novel, uses the theme of red-shirted Star Fleet officers as <a href="/wiki/Cannon_fodder" title="Cannon fodder">cannon fodder</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Traumschiff_Surprise_%E2%80%93_Periode_1" title="Traumschiff Surprise – Periode 1"><i>(T)raumschiff Surprise – Periode 1</i></a> (2004) is a movie directed by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Herbig" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael Herbig">Michael Herbig</a> which parodies <i>Star Trek</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Fan_productions">Fan productions</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Fan productions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_fan_productions" title="Star Trek fan productions">Star Trek fan productions</a></div>
<p><i>Star Trek</i> has inspired many fans to produce stories for free Internet distribution. Many of these are set in the time of <i>The Original Series</i>, including <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Phase_II_(fan_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Star Trek: Phase II (fan series)">Star Trek: Phase II</a></i> which was nominated for a Hugo Award and received support from actors and writers who were involved with <i>The Original Series</i>.
</p><p>"<a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_Continues" title="Star Trek Continues">Star Trek: Continues</a>" chronicles the last year of the 5-year voyage of The Enterprise. Gene Roddenberry's son, "Rod", announced after a showing in 2014 that this series would have been considered canon by his father.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Comprising 11 full episodes and numerous additional materials, <i>Star Trek: Continues</i> was produced from 2013 to 2017 and funded by a kickstarter.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Series_sequels">Series sequels</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Series sequels"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Star_Trek_television_series" title="List of Star Trek television series">List of Star Trek television series</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:QTXP_20121019_Destination_Star_Trek_London_MG_2284.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/QTXP_20121019_Destination_Star_Trek_London_MG_2284.jpg/250px-QTXP_20121019_Destination_Star_Trek_London_MG_2284.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/QTXP_20121019_Destination_Star_Trek_London_MG_2284.jpg/500px-QTXP_20121019_Destination_Star_Trek_London_MG_2284.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a><figcaption>The Captains, together in London at <i>Destination Star Trek</i></figcaption></figure>
<p>The original <i>Star Trek</i> was followed in 1973 and beyond with more shows set in the same <a href="/wiki/Shared_universe" title="Shared universe">shared universe</a>. The subsequent series include:
</p>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Animated_Series" title="Star Trek: The Animated Series">The Animated Series</a></i> (1973–1974)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation" title="Star Trek: The Next Generation">The Next Generation</a></i> (1987–1994, <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_(film_series)#The_Next_Generation_films" class="mw-redirect" title="Star Trek (film series)">films</a>)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Deep_Space_Nine" title="Star Trek: Deep Space Nine">Deep Space Nine</a></i> (1993–1999)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Voyager" title="Star Trek: Voyager">Voyager</a></i> (1995–2001)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Enterprise" title="Star Trek: Enterprise">Enterprise</a></i> (2001–2005)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Discovery" title="Star Trek: Discovery">Discovery</a></i> (2017–2024)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Short_Treks" title="Star Trek: Short Treks">Star Trek: Short Treks</a></i> (2018–2020)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Picard" title="Star Trek: Picard">Picard</a></i> (2020–2023)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Lower_Decks" title="Star Trek: Lower Decks">Lower Decks</a></i> (2020–2024)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Prodigy" title="Star Trek: Prodigy">Prodigy</a></i> (2021–present)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Very_Short_Treks" title="Star Trek: Very Short Treks">Very Short Treks</a></i> (2023)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Strange_New_Worlds" title="Star Trek: Strange New Worlds">Strange New Worlds</a></i> (2022–present)</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Reception">Reception</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Reception"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rod_Serling" title="Rod Serling">Rod Serling</a> said of the series that "<i>Star Trek</i> was again a very inconsistent show which at times sparkled with true ingenuity and pure science fiction approaches. At other times it was more carnival-like, and very much more the creature of television than the creature of a legitimate literary form."<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Isaac_Asimov" title="Isaac Asimov">Isaac Asimov</a> and <i>Star Trek</i> creator Gene Roddenberry developed a unique relationship during <i>Star Trek</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s initial run in the late 1960s. Asimov wrote a critical essay on <i>Star Trek</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s scientific accuracy for <i>TV Guide</i> magazine. Roddenberry retorted respectfully with a personal letter explaining the limitations of accuracy when writing a weekly series. Asimov corrected himself with a follow-up essay to <i>TV Guide</i> claiming despite its inaccuracies, that <i>Star Trek</i> was a fresh and intellectually challenging science fiction television show. The two remained friends to the point where Asimov even served as an adviser on a number of <i>Star Trek</i> projects.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On <a href="/wiki/Review_aggregator" title="Review aggregator">review aggregator</a> <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a>, Season 1 received an approval rating of 92% based on 24 reviews, with an average rating of 9/10. The critical consensus reads, "An optimistic ode to humanity, <i>Star Trek</i> may look dated, but its gadgetry and solid storytelling solidify its place as one of pop culture's most enduring franchises."<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Season 2 received an approval rating of 100% based on 6 reviews, with an average rating of 7.33/10.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Season 3 received an approval rating of 50% based on 10 reviews, with an average rating of 5.5/10. The critical consensus reads, "Budget cuts leave the stars of <i>Star Trek</i> stranded among shoddy set pieces and clunky writing – though even at its worst fans may still enjoy its campy delights."<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, in a listing that included each <i>Star Trek</i> film and TV series together, this series was ranked first by the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times"><i>L.A. Times</i></a>, ahead of the 1982 film <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_II:_The_Wrath_of_Khan" title="Star Trek II: The Wrath of Khan">Star Trek II: The Wrath of Khan</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Deep_Space_Nine" title="Star Trek: Deep Space Nine">Star Trek: Deep Space Nine</a></i>, in third place.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, <a href="/wiki/Vulture.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Vulture.com">Vulture</a> ranked the original <i>Star Trek</i> the third best live-action <i>Star Trek</i> television show, while at the same time praising it for "laying down the foundation".<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>In 2018, <i><a href="/wiki/IndieWire" title="IndieWire">IndieWire</a></i> ranked <i>Star Trek</i> the original series as the 8th best space science fiction show set in outer space, including 18 overall shows from this genre.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, <a href="/wiki/Io9" title="Io9">Io9</a>/<a href="/wiki/Gizmodo" title="Gizmodo">Gizmodo</a> ranked the fictional spacecraft design shown in this television series, the Enterprise, as the number one best version of starship <i>Enterprise</i> of the <i>Star Trek</i> franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-162"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> They felt that the original design was still superior to almost a dozen different later versions.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-162"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019, <a href="/wiki/Nerdist_News" title="Nerdist News"><i>Nerdist</i></a> ranked the original series number one best out of seven <i>Star Trek</i> franchise television series, including up to the second season of <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Discovery" title="Star Trek: Discovery">Star Trek: Discovery</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019, <a href="/wiki/Popular_Mechanics" title="Popular Mechanics">Popular Mechanics</a> ranked <i>Star Trek</i> the 6th best science fiction television show ever.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2021, <a href="/wiki/Empire_(magazine)" title="Empire (magazine)"><i>Empire</i> magazine</a> ranked it the 36th greatest television show ever.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-165"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
